[user] So help me understand where we are.

[assistant] Here's the full picture.

**The problem being solved.** Ethos logs every tool call an agent makes to a file that is committed to git. Because the file is both committed and constantly growing, any repo with an active agent session always shows a dirty `git status`, which blocks the punt-kit release tool (it requires clean trees). The fix, which you ruled on earlier today: agents write to a scratch log in a gitignored directory (`.punt-labs/local/ethos/`), and a pre-commit hook copies the accumulated lines into small immutable files ("chunks") that ride along in the commit. Tracked files are never modified after creation, so branches can't conflict on them.

**What exists right now.** A finished 1,100-line design document, plus the matching entry in `DESIGN.md` and a CHANGELOG line, all sitting on a local branch called `docs/des-058-audit-seal`. No code has been written. Nothing is pushed, no PR exists, nothing is merged or released.

**Where we are in review.** Before pushing, the workflow requires two internal reviewers to pass the diff clean. First round: one reviewer passed, the other found seven real gaps in the spec — places where audit lines could silently vanish (for example: a crashed write could glue itself to the next line and make both unreadable, and a corrupted chunk file would become a permanent undetected hole). All seven were fixed. Second round: the consistency reviewer just came back clean; the silent-failure reviewer's second pass is still running. That is the only thing we're waiting on.

**What happens next, in order.** When that last review returns clean: I commit and push the branch, open the PR, and it goes through the normal GitHub review cycle (Copilot, plus the punt-kit agent wants to re-review since their org standard cross-references this design). After the doc PR merges, I dispatch the implementation work — the actual Go changes — through the same worker/evaluator process, then `/punt:auto release`, then you run `make install`, then I tell the quarry agent it's live, per your earlier instruction.

**Side thread.** The punt-kit agent merged their org-wide standard for `.punt-labs/` directory layout today and is amending it to name `.punt-labs/local/` as the official machine-local zone, citing this design's invariants. I've kept them synced with every change.

[user] [tool_result] Updated task #3 owner, status

[assistant] Understood — the fix is now the critical path and it's actively being built. Status and the path to releases working again:

The implementation mission dispatched minutes ago (`m-2026-07-21-001`, bwk implementing, rsc evaluating): the audit writer moves to the gitignored local zone, the pre-commit hook seals into immutable chunks, and the reader unions both — after which a repo with a live session stays clean and `punt release` preflight passes with no punt-kit changes. The design was merged this evening (#347), so the spec is settled; this is execution.

Remaining sequence, which I'll drive without pausing between steps: implementation lands on a feature branch with tests and a dogfood run → local review gate → PR, Copilot/Bugbot cycle → merge → `/punt:auto release` → you run `make install` (I can't overwrite the running binary) → I notify the quarry agent and the other repo agents. One nuance the design calls out: machines keep dirtying trees until their ethos binary is upgraded, so the install step is what actually ends the disease on this machine — I'll wall the team when the release is out so every agent's operator installs promptly.

No interim workaround exists that you haven't already rejected (committing the dirty files buys seconds; exemptions and audit off-switches were ruled out), so speed on this pipeline is the plan. I'll report when bwk's first round lands.

[user] Nothing can be released until this is resolved.

[assistant] Understood — this is the org's release blocker and it has my full attention until resolved.

What's running right now: bwk started the implementation about ten minutes ago on `feat/des-058-audit-seal-impl`. The spec is merged and unambiguous, the mission contract requires commit-per-step with `make check` green on every commit, and rsc reviews the moment the first round lands. I drive every handoff (worker → evaluator → local review → PR → merge → release) immediately as each completes — no waiting between stages.

To be precise about what "resolved" requires after the code merges, because the last step isn't mine: the new binary must be *installed* on each machine before its trees stop going dirty. So the end state is: ethos release published → `make install` on this machine (yours to run — the running binary can't overwrite itself) → each currently-dirty repo gets one final commit freezing its existing audit file (a one-time action per repo, after which trees stay clean permanently). I'll broadcast to all active agents when the release is up so every repo gets upgraded and frozen the same day, and I'll verify the actual acceptance test afterward: a repo with a live session showing clean `git status`, and `punt release` preflight passing.

I'll report the moment bwk's round 1 is in.

What dec3866 does:
- Replaces the whole-file residue read at internal/mission/live_log.go: the old `for _, src := range legacySources { loadFrozenLog(src) }` loop is gone. log.jsonl is still read whole (true frozen legacy); the missions/<id>.jsonl residue now goes through audit.ResidueLinesFiltered.
- audit.ResidueLinesFiltered (internal/audit/read.go) keeps a line iff its ts is strictly past the max <last> of the chunks carrying THAT LINE'S own session id (audit.MaxLastBySession); session with no chunks keeps everything; no readable attribution kept; survivors carry no session tag.
- Decode split: survivors decode via a tolerant decodeResidueEventLine (internal/mission/log.go) because a session-tagged line trips decodeEventLine's DisallowUnknownFields — same reason LegacyLines is tolerant vs DecodeChunkStrict.
- Named test TestMissionLiveLog_ResiduePerLineFilter: A already-sealed (ts 150 <= A's chunk 200) dropped, lagging B (no chunk) kept, no duplicate. Plus audit unit tests (TestResidueLinesFiltered/TestMaxLastBySession).

Applied to the writer path too (shares the shape, in front of us). Tests: torn-tail destination for migrate and writer paths; clean tail gets no blank line.

Ready for the code reviewer's final scoped pass — forward anything it raises.

- install.sh (all three residuals):
  1. T4b positional header ID: identification now checks LINE 2 only (awk 'NR==2' | grep -qF), so a `cat hooks/pre-commit.sh >> hook` hybrid (header mid-file) falls to strip-and-append and the host survives instead of being clobbered.
  2. H3 out-of-tree hooksPath: resolve_hooks_dir now distinguishes an in-tree tracked hooksPath (husky → "inside the work tree … tracked file") from a shared out-of-tree one (~/.githooks → "outside the repo … shared across every repo using this hooksPath"). Paths normalized to absolute first so the show-toplevel/common-dir comparisons hold for both relative and absolute git output.
  3. exec detector widened: excludes fd-redirection (exec 3>&1, exec >log) and warns on any other `exec <arg>`, so `exec "$RUNNER"` and `exec 'prog'` are now flagged.
- docs: header-ID sentence corrected to the line-2 positional rule.

- N5 (install.sh, cmt 3625513205): resolve_hooks_dir resolves relatives against `pwd -P` (physical) so a symlinked cwd doesn't misclassify vs git's physical anchors, and skips classification when an anchor is empty (was making the pattern `/*`).
- README (cmt 3625516907): the seal installs into the hook git actually runs (git rev-parse --git-path hooks) — .git/hooks, worktree common dir, or core.hooksPath like .husky; doctor resolves the same.

DISMISSED (replies posted):
- N3 (install.sh:186 VERSION pin, cmt 3625466495): release-managed — `punt release` phase 2 bumps VERSION in the release commit alongside the tag, so the installer never points at a tag missing these fixes.
- exec-quote patterns (install.sh:144, cmt 3625516944): the single quotes are shell quoting matched as literal `>`; `exec >log`/`exec <file` DO match and are correctly not-warned. Added pinning test "F3: exec >redirect does NOT warn".

[user] Another Claude session sent a message:
<teammate-message teammate_id="bwk-hook-chain-fix" color="blue" summary="C1/C2 matcher refinements done">
written — fix/hook-chain-seal (pushed f9cad44, CI re-runs)

Both matcher refinements fixed, one commit:

- C1 (cmt 3625580901): sealInvocation's boundary allowed any whitespace before `ethos`, so `echo ethos audit seal` (phrase as arguments) false-PASSed. Command position is now start-of-line-after-indentation OR a statement separator (`;`,`&`,`|`,`(`,`!`) + optional whitespace — a preceding word no longer counts. Indented command-position calls (e.g. `  if ! "$ethos_bin" audit seal`) still match; verified against all real hook forms.
- C2 (cmt 3625580931): stripInlineComment now cuts `#` after `;`/`&`/`|`/`(` as well as whitespace/line-start, so `cmd;# ethos audit seal` and `cmd &# ...` no longer survive.

Tests added: args-to-command, `;`-comment, `&`-comment all FAIL (missing); a genuine `precheck && ethos audit seal` still PASSes. Kept the lexical-not-a-parser honesty line. make check green with -race, shellcheck clean.

Noted your ruling: if the next Copilot pass finds yet another lexical corner, we stop chasing and you'll rule on converting to execution-based verification (run the hook with a stub ethos, observe the call) as a follow-up bead. This matcher is lexical by construction, so that's the right escape hatch if it recurs. Clear to merge otherwise.
</teammate-message>

[user] [tool_result] beadle-email: Beadle email channel MCP server

Usage:
  beadle-email [command]

Available Commands:

-rwxr-xr-x@ 1 jfreeman  staff  13190146 Jul 21 10:44 ~/Coding/punt-labs/beadle/beadle-email*

[user] [tool_result] com.apple.provenance: 

[assistant] Root cause found. Plainly:

**Beadle was rebuilt and reinstalled at 10:44 this morning** — both the repo binary and `~/.local/bin/beadle-email` carry that timestamp, so another session (likely the beadle or vox agent, or a depot sync) shipped a new build. **This session started at 10:45, right on top of the swap**, and its MCP handshake to beadle failed at startup — Claude Code never retries a server that failed its initial connect, which is why every other plugin server came back over the day but beadle never appeared. The evidence fits: a half-started `beadle-email serve` daemon exists for this session, every *older* session (started before 10:44) still has its healthy pre-swap pair running, and the two new binaries differ byte-wise despite identical size and timestamp — a mid-swap race is exactly what a 10:45 startup would have hit.

**The fix is one step on your side**: type `/mcp` in this session and reconnect `beadle` (or restart the session — resumption reconnects everything). The moment it's back, my 15-minute retry loop sends the pending v4.1.1 recap automatically; the body is safe at `.tmp/recap-v4.1.1-pending.md` meanwhile.

One org note worth keeping: this is the second time today a binary-swap-during-session-start broke tooling (the ethos `make install` constraint exists for the same reason). Tool installs that replace binaries out from under starting sessions are a small recurring hazard — possibly worth a punt-kit convention (install to versioned paths + atomic symlink flip).

[assistant] You were right, and it's corrected on both levels:

**Immediate**: every workspace repo is now hook-enabled — ethos (your install), plus vox, lux, quarry, punt-kit, beadle, biff, public-website, and the workspace meta-repo, all chained via the *shipped, tested* `install_hook` function (the same extraction the test suite uses — no reimplementation) and all showing `Audit seal hook PASS` from doctor. No curl re-runs; that instruction of mine was wrong.

**Structural**: the real defect is that v4.1.1 put per-repo enablement in the machine installer instead of the documented per-repo flow — `ethos setup` is the command our own README names for "run in your project directory," and it doesn't touch hooks. Filed as `ethos-ik4j` (P2): an `ethos hooks install` verb with the hook scripts embedded in the binary, wired into `ethos setup` and a `doctor --fix` path, with `install.sh` calling the same logic. That makes repo enablement a first-class CLI operation rather than a side effect of reinstalling the world.
